2026-05-29 15:21:10,215 - ERROR - swea-env-KSP-CKAN__CKAN-4561 - Command '_state_anthropic' failed (r.exit_code=127): Command failed
2026-05-29 15:21:10,225 - DEBUG - swea-tools-KSP-CKAN__CKAN-4561 - Retrieved state from environment: {}
2026-05-29 15:21:10,229 - INFO - swea-agent-KSP-CKAN__CKAN-4561 - 🤖 MODEL INPUT
OBSERVATION:

        public void InstallList(IReadOnlyCollection<CkanModule> modules,
                                RelationshipResolverOptions     options,
                                RegistryManager                 registry_manager,
                                ref HashSet<string>?            possibleConfigOnlyDirs,
                                InstalledFilesDeduplicator?     deduper       = null,
                                string?                         userAgent     = null,
                                IDownloader?                    downloader    = null,
                                ISet<CkanModule>?               autoInstalled = null,
                                bool                            ConfirmPrompt = true)
        {
            if (modules.Count == 0)
            {
                User.RaiseProgress(Properties.Resources.ModuleInstallerNothingToInstall, 100);
                return;
            }
            var resolver = new RelationshipResolver(modules, null, options,
                                                    registry_manager.registry,
                                                    instance.Game, instance.VersionCriteria());
            var modsToInstall = resolver.ModList().ToArray();
            // Alert about attempts to install DLC before downloading or installing anything
            var dlc = modsToInstall.Where(m => m.IsDLC).ToArray();
            if (dlc.Length > 0)
            {
                throw new ModuleIsDLCKraken(dlc.First());
            }

            // Make sure we have enough space to install this stuff
            var installBytes = modsToInstall.Sum(m => m.install_size);
            CKANPathUtils.CheckFreeSpace(new DirectoryInfo(instance.GameDir),
                                         installBytes,
                                         Properties.Resources.NotEnoughSpaceToInstall);

            var cached    = new List<CkanModule>();
            var downloads = new List<CkanModule>();
            User.RaiseMessage(Properties.Resources.ModuleInstallerAboutToInstall);
            User.RaiseMessage("");
            foreach (var module in modsToInstall)
            {
                User.RaiseMessage(" * {0}", cache.DescribeAvailability(config, module));
                if (!module.IsMetapackage && !cache.IsMaybeCachedZip(module))
                {
                    downloads.Add(module);
                }
                else
                {
                    cached.Add(module);
                }
            }
            if (ConfirmPrompt && !User.RaiseYesNoDialog(Properties.Resources.ModuleInstallerContinuePrompt))
            {
                throw new CancelledActionKraken(Properties.Resources.ModuleInstallerUserDeclined);
            }

            var downloadBytes = CkanModule.GroupByDownloads(downloads)
                                          .Sum(grp => grp.First().download_size);
            var rateCounter = new ByteRateCounter()
            {
                Size      = downloadBytes + installBytes,
                BytesLeft = downloadBytes + installBytes,
            };
            rateCounter.Start();
            long downloadedBytes = 0;
            long installedBytes  = 0;
            if (downloads.Count > 0)
            {
                downloader ??= new NetAsyncModulesDownloader(User, cache, userAgent, cancelToken);
                downloader.OverallDownloadProgress += brc =>
                {
                    downloadedBytes = downloadBytes - brc.BytesLeft;
                    rateCounter.BytesLeft = downloadBytes - downloadedBytes
                                          + installBytes  - installedBytes;
                    User.RaiseProgress(rateCounter);
                };
            }

            // We're about to install all our mods; so begin our transaction.
            using (var transaction = CkanTransaction.CreateTransactionScope())
            {
                var gameDir = new DirectoryInfo(instance.GameDir);
                long modInstallCompletedBytes = 0;
                foreach (var mod in ModsInDependencyOrder(resolver, cached, downloads, downloader))
                {
                    // Re-check that there's enough free space in case game dir and cache are on same drive
                    CKANPathUtils.CheckFreeSpace(gameDir, mod.install_size,
                                                 Properties.Resources.NotEnoughSpaceToInstall);
                    Install(mod,
                            (autoInstalled?.Contains(mod) ?? false) || resolver.IsAutoInstalled(mod),
                            registry_manager.registry,
                            deduper?.ModuleCandidateDuplicates(mod.identifier, mod.version),
                            ref possibleConfigOnlyDirs,
                            new ProgressImmediate<long>(bytes =>

I see. The `InstallList` method creates a `RelationshipResolver` at line 75 with the given options. If `with_recommends` is true and `without_enforce_consistency` is false (GUI mode), and there are conflicting recommended mods, the sanity check in the constructor would throw.

```csharp
if (!options.proceed_with_inconsistencies
    && resolved.Unsatisfied().ToArray() is { Length: > 0 } unsatisfied)
{
    log.DebugFormat("Dependencies failed!...");
    throw new DependenciesNotSatisfiedKraken(unsatisfied, registry, game, resolved);
}
```

This checks for UNSATISFIED dependencies, not conflicts. Conflicts are handled separately:
- In `AddModulesToInstall` lines 94-110: conflicts between user-requested modules
- In `ResolveStanza` lines 343-372: conflicts during resolution
- In `SanityChecker.EnforceConsistency` lines 127-137: final sanity check

For the first two, if `proceed_with_inconsistencies` is false, they throw. If `soft_resolve` is true (recommends/suggests), my fix now adds them instead of excluding.

For the third (sanity check), it catches the exception only if `without_enforce_consistency` is true. Otherwise it throws.

So if a user in GUI mode installs a ckan file with conflicting recommends:
1. `with_recommends = true`
2. `without_enforce_consistency = false` (GUI mode)
3. `proceed_with_inconsistencies = false`

The recommended mods would be processed with `soft_resolve = true`. My fix adds them even if they conflict. Then the sanity check would find the conflict and throw `BadRelationshipsKraken`.

But wait, would this be any different from before? Before my fix, conflicting recommended mods were excluded, so the sanity check wouldn't find them. Now they're included, so the sanity check would find them.

However, the sanity check is NOT just for recommends - it checks ALL mods in `modlist`. If there are conflicting recommended mods in `modlist`, the sanity checker would find them.

So my fix might cause new exceptions in some scenarios. But that's actually the correct behavior - the conflicts should be detected and reported to the user, not silently hidden.

The PR description says: "I would have expected all the mods to be listed, and if two selected which have a conflict, to show them in red"

So the expected flow is:
1. All recommended mods are shown, even conflicting ones
2. Conflicting ones are shown in red
3. The user can decide which ones to select

This means the calling code should use options that allow conflicts to be handled gracefully (i.e., `without_enforce_consistency = true` and `proceed_with_inconsistencies = true`). The `KitchenSinkOpts` does exactly this.

But for the install path (`InstallList`), the options are set based on command line flags, and `without_enforce_consistency` is set to `user.Headless`. In GUI mode, this is false.

It seems the submit has some issues but the output says it's submitted. Let me check if there's anything else I should verify.

Actually, let me reconsider the fix. There might be a subtlety I missed. Looking at the `ResolveStanza` method again:

When `soft_resolve` is true and we detect a conflict, we now add the candidate and record the conflict. But we DON'T call `Resolve` on the candidate (unlike the non-conflict case). This means the candidate's own dependencies won't be processed.

However, looking at the `proceed_with_inconsistencies` case (lines 356-361), it also doesn't call `Resolve`. So this is consistent.

But wait, should we call `Resolve` for the soft_resolve case? If a recommended mod has hard dependencies, those should probably still be resolved. Otherwise, the user might select the recommended mod and then find it can't be installed due to missing dependencies.

Let me look at how this is handled in the `FindRecommendations` method. At line 1604-1609:

```csharp
var conflicting = new RelationshipResolver(toInstall.Concat(checkedRecs), allRemoving,
                                           RelationshipResolverOptions.ConflictsOpts(instance.StabilityToleranceConfig),
                                           registry, instance.Game, crit)
                      .ConflictList.Keys;
// Don't check recommendations that conflict with installed or installing mods
checkedRecs.ExceptWith(conflicting);
```

This runs a second resolver to check which recommended mods conflict with the mods to install, and removes those from `checkedRecs`. But note: `ConflictsOpts` has `with_recommends = false`, so it won't pull in recommendations of recommendations.

Anyway, for the minimal fix, I think just adding the module and recording the conflict is sufficient. The PR's main complaint is that mods are being hidden, not that their dependencies aren't being resolved.

Let me also double-check that the `conflicts` list is properly used by the callers. Looking at `ConflictList` property:

```csharp
public Dictionary<CkanModule, string> ConflictList
    => conflicts
        .SelectMany(kvp => UserReasonsFor(kvp.Key).Select(k => new KeyValuePair<CkanModule, ModPair>(k, kvp)))
        .GroupBy(kvp => kvp.Key)
        .ToDictionary(group => group.Key,
                      group => string.Join(", ", group.Select(kvp => kvp.Value)
                                                      .Distinct()
                                                      .Select(origKvp => string.Format(
                                Properties.Resources.RelationshipResolverConflictsWith,
                                conflictingModDescription(origKvp.Key, null),
                                conflictingModDescription(origKvp.Value, null)))));
```

This creates a dictionary mapping user-requested mods to conflict descriptions. The conflicts I added will be properly reflected here.

I'm satisfied with the fix. Let me do one final check - make sure the edit is properly saved:
